4563    /**
4564     * Invoked when a column is repositioned. If a cell is being
4565     * edited, then editing is stopped and the cell is redrawn.
4566     * <p>
4567     * Application code will not use these methods explicitly, they
4568     * are used internally by JTable.
4569     *
4570     * @param e   the event received
4571     * @see TableColumnModelListener
4572     */
4573    public void columnMoved(TableColumnModelEvent e) {
4574        if (isEditing() && !getCellEditor().stopCellEditing()) {
4575            getCellEditor().cancelCellEditing();
4576        }
4577        repaint();
4578    }
4579
4580    /**
4581     * Invoked when a column is moved due to a margin change.
4582     * If a cell is being edited, then editing is stopped and the cell
4583     * is redrawn.
4584     * <p>
4585     * Application code will not use these methods explicitly, they
4586     * are used internally by JTable.
4587     *
4588     * @param  e    the event received
4589     * @see TableColumnModelListener
4590     */
4591    public void columnMarginChanged(ChangeEvent e) {
4592        if (isEditing() && !getCellEditor().stopCellEditing()) {
4593            getCellEditor().cancelCellEditing();
4594        }
4595        TableColumn resizingColumn = getResizingColumn();
4596        // Need to do this here, before the parent's
4597        // layout manager calls getPreferredSize().
4598        if (resizingColumn != null && autoResizeMode == AUTO_RESIZE_OFF) {
4599            resizingColumn.setPreferredWidth(resizingColumn.getWidth());
4600        }
4601        resizeAndRepaint();
4602    }
4603
4604    private int limit(int i, int a, int b) {
4605        return Math.min(b, Math.max(i, a));
4606    }
4607
4608    /**
4609     * Invoked when the selection model of the <code>TableColumnModel</code>
4610     * is changed.
4611     * <p>
4612     * Application code will not use these methods explicitly, they
4613     * are used internally by JTable.
4614     *
4615     * @param  e  the event received
4616     * @see TableColumnModelListener
4617     */
4618    public void columnSelectionChanged(ListSelectionEvent e) {
4619        boolean isAdjusting = e.getValueIsAdjusting();
4620        if (columnSelectionAdjusting && !isAdjusting) {
4621            // The assumption is that when the model is no longer adjusting
4622            // we will have already gotten all the changes, and therefore
4623            // don't need to do an additional paint.
4624            columnSelectionAdjusting = false;
4625            return;
4626        }
4627        columnSelectionAdjusting = isAdjusting;
4628        // The getCellRect() call will fail unless there is at least one row.
4629        if (getRowCount() <= 0 || getColumnCount() <= 0) {
4630            return;
4631        }
4632        int firstIndex = limit(e.getFirstIndex(), 0, getColumnCount()-1);
4633        int lastIndex = limit(e.getLastIndex(), 0, getColumnCount()-1);
4634        int minRow = 0;
4635        int maxRow = getRowCount() - 1;
4636        if (getRowSelectionAllowed()) {
4637            minRow = selectionModel.getMinSelectionIndex();
4638            maxRow = selectionModel.getMaxSelectionIndex();
4639            int leadRow = getAdjustedIndex(selectionModel.getLeadSelectionIndex(), true);
4640
4641            if (minRow == -1 || maxRow == -1) {
4642                if (leadRow == -1) {
4643                    // nothing to repaint, return
4644                    return;
4645                }
4646
4647                // only thing to repaint is the lead
4648                minRow = maxRow = leadRow;
4649            } else {
4650                // We need to consider more than just the range between
4651                // the min and max selected index. The lead row, which could
4652                // be outside this range, should be considered also.
4653                if (leadRow != -1) {
4654                    minRow = Math.min(minRow, leadRow);
4655                    maxRow = Math.max(maxRow, leadRow);
4656                }
4657            }
4658        }
4659        Rectangle firstColumnRect = getCellRect(minRow, firstIndex, false);
4660        Rectangle lastColumnRect = getCellRect(maxRow, lastIndex, false);
4661        Rectangle dirtyRegion = firstColumnRect.union(lastColumnRect);
4662        repaint(dirtyRegion);
4663    }
4664
4665//
4666// Implementing ListSelectionListener interface
4667//
4668
4669    /**
4670     * Invoked when the row selection changes -- repaints to show the new
4671     * selection.
4672     * <p>
4673     * Application code will not use these methods explicitly, they
4674     * are used internally by JTable.
4675     *
4676     * @param e   the event received
4677     * @see ListSelectionListener
4678     */
4679    public void valueChanged(ListSelectionEvent e) {
4680        if (sortManager != null) {
4681            sortManager.viewSelectionChanged(e);
4682        }
4683        boolean isAdjusting = e.getValueIsAdjusting();
4684        if (rowSelectionAdjusting && !isAdjusting) {
4685            // The assumption is that when the model is no longer adjusting
4686            // we will have already gotten all the changes, and therefore
4687            // don't need to do an additional paint.
4688            rowSelectionAdjusting = false;
4689            return;
4690        }
4691        rowSelectionAdjusting = isAdjusting;
4692        // The getCellRect() calls will fail unless there is at least one column.
4693        if (getRowCount() <= 0 || getColumnCount() <= 0) {
4694            return;
4695        }
4696        int firstIndex = limit(e.getFirstIndex(), 0, getRowCount()-1);
4697        int lastIndex = limit(e.getLastIndex(), 0, getRowCount()-1);
4698        Rectangle firstRowRect = getCellRect(firstIndex, 0, false);
4699        Rectangle lastRowRect = getCellRect(lastIndex, getColumnCount()-1, false);
4700        Rectangle dirtyRegion = firstRowRect.union(lastRowRect);
4701        repaint(dirtyRegion);
4702    }

4708    /**
4709     * Invoked when editing is finished. The changes are saved and the
4710     * editor is discarded.
4711     * <p>
4712     * Application code will not use these methods explicitly, they
4713     * are used internally by JTable.
4714     *
4715     * @param  e  the event received
4716     * @see CellEditorListener
4717     */
4718    public void editingStopped(ChangeEvent e) {
4719        // Take in the new value
4720        TableCellEditor editor = getCellEditor();
4721        if (editor != null) {
4722            Object value = editor.getCellEditorValue();
4723            setValueAt(value, editingRow, editingColumn);
4724            removeEditor();
4725        }
4726    }

4734     *
4735     * @param  e  the event received
4736     * @see CellEditorListener
4737     */
4738    public void editingCanceled(ChangeEvent e) {

4750     *              <code>JViewport</code> whose view is this table
4751     * @see Scrollable#getPreferredScrollableViewportSize
4752     * @beaninfo
4753     * description: The preferred size of the viewport.
4754     */

4759    /**
4760     * Returns the preferred size of the viewport for this table.
4761     *
4762     * @return a <code>Dimension</code> object containing the <code>preferredSize</code> of the <code>JViewport</code>
4763     *         which displays this table
4764     * @see Scrollable#getPreferredScrollableViewportSize
4765     */
4766    public Dimension getPreferredScrollableViewportSize() {
4767        return preferredViewportSize;
4768    }
4769
4770    /**
4771     * Returns the scroll increment (in pixels) that completely exposes one new
4772     * row or column (depending on the orientation).
4773     * <p>
4774     * This method is called each time the user requests a unit scroll.
4775     *
4776     * @param visibleRect the view area visible within the viewport
4777     * @param orientation either <code>SwingConstants.VERTICAL</code>
4778     *                  or <code>SwingConstants.HORIZONTAL</code>
4779     * @param direction less than zero to scroll up/left,
4780     *                  greater than zero for down/right
4781     * @return the "unit" increment for scrolling in the specified direction
4782     * @see Scrollable#getScrollableUnitIncrement
4783     */
4784    public int getScrollableUnitIncrement(Rectangle visibleRect,
4785                                          int orientation,
4786                                          int direction) {
4787        int leadingRow;
4788        int leadingCol;
4789        Rectangle leadingCellRect;
4790
4791        int leadingVisibleEdge;
4792        int leadingCellEdge;
4793        int leadingCellSize;
4794
4795        leadingRow = getLeadingRow(visibleRect);
4796        leadingCol = getLeadingCol(visibleRect);
4797        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL && leadingRow < 0) {
4798            // Couldn't find leading row - return some default value
4799            return getRowHeight();
4800        }
4801        else if (orientation == SwingConstants.HORIZONTAL && leadingCol < 0) {
4802            // Couldn't find leading col - return some default value
4803            return 100;
4804        }
4805
4806        // Note that it's possible for one of leadingCol or leadingRow to be
4807        // -1, depending on the orientation.  This is okay, as getCellRect()
4808        // still provides enough information to calculate the unit increment.
4809        leadingCellRect = getCellRect(leadingRow, leadingCol, true);
4810        leadingVisibleEdge = leadingEdge(visibleRect, orientation);
4811        leadingCellEdge = leadingEdge(leadingCellRect, orientation);
4812
4813        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL) {
4814            leadingCellSize = leadingCellRect.height;
4815
4816        }
4817        else {
4818            leadingCellSize = leadingCellRect.width;
4819        }
4820
4821        // 4 cases:
4822        // #1: Leading cell fully visible, reveal next cell
4823        // #2: Leading cell fully visible, hide leading cell
4824        // #3: Leading cell partially visible, hide rest of leading cell
4825        // #4: Leading cell partially visible, reveal rest of leading cell
4826
4827        if (leadingVisibleEdge == leadingCellEdge) { // Leading cell is fully
4828                                                     // visible
4829            // Case #1: Reveal previous cell
4830            if (direction < 0) {
4831                int retVal = 0;
4832
4833                if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL) {
4834                    // Loop past any zero-height rows
4835                    while (--leadingRow >= 0) {
4836                        retVal = getRowHeight(leadingRow);
4837                        if (retVal != 0) {
4838                            break;
4839                        }
4840                    }
4841                }
4842                else { // HORIZONTAL
4843                    // Loop past any zero-width cols
4844                    while (--leadingCol >= 0) {
4845                        retVal = getCellRect(leadingRow, leadingCol, true).width;
4846                        if (retVal != 0) {
4847                            break;
4848                        }
4849                    }
4850                }
4851                return retVal;
4852            }
4853            else { // Case #2: hide leading cell
4854                return leadingCellSize;
4855            }
4856        }
4857        else { // Leading cell is partially hidden
4858            // Compute visible, hidden portions
4859            int hiddenAmt = Math.abs(leadingVisibleEdge - leadingCellEdge);
4860            int visibleAmt = leadingCellSize - hiddenAmt;
4861
4862            if (direction > 0) {
4863                // Case #3: hide showing portion of leading cell
4864                return visibleAmt;
4865            }
4866            else { // Case #4: reveal hidden portion of leading cell
4867                return hiddenAmt;
4868            }
4869        }
4870    }
4871
4872    /**
4873     * Returns <code>visibleRect.height</code> or
4874     * <code>visibleRect.width</code>,
4875     * depending on this table's orientation.  Note that as of Swing 1.1.1
4876     * (Java 2 v 1.2.2) the value
4877     * returned will ensure that the viewport is cleanly aligned on
4878     * a row boundary.
4879     *
4880     * @return <code>visibleRect.height</code> or
4881     *                                  <code>visibleRect.width</code>
4882     *                                  per the orientation
4883     * @see Scrollable#getScrollableBlockIncrement
4884     */
4885    public int getScrollableBlockIncrement(Rectangle visibleRect,
4886            int orientation, int direction) {
4887
4888        if (getRowCount() == 0) {
4889            // Short-circuit empty table model
4890            if (SwingConstants.VERTICAL == orientation) {
4891                int rh = getRowHeight();
4892                return (rh > 0) ? Math.max(rh, (visibleRect.height / rh) * rh) :
4893                                  visibleRect.height;
4894            }
4895            else {
4896                return visibleRect.width;
4897            }
4898        }
4899        // Shortcut for vertical scrolling of a table w/ uniform row height
4900        if (null == rowModel && SwingConstants.VERTICAL == orientation) {
4901            int row = rowAtPoint(visibleRect.getLocation());
4902            assert row != -1;
4903            int col = columnAtPoint(visibleRect.getLocation());
4904            Rectangle cellRect = getCellRect(row, col, true);
4905
4906            if (cellRect.y == visibleRect.y) {
4907                int rh = getRowHeight();
4908                assert rh > 0;
4909                return Math.max(rh, (visibleRect.height / rh) * rh);
4910            }
4911        }
4912        if (direction < 0) {
4913            return getPreviousBlockIncrement(visibleRect, orientation);
4914        }
4915        else {
4916            return getNextBlockIncrement(visibleRect, orientation);
4917        }
4918    }
4919
4920    /**
4921     * Called to get the block increment for upward scrolling in cases of
4922     * horizontal scrolling, or for vertical scrolling of a table with
4923     * variable row heights.
4924     */
4925    private int getPreviousBlockIncrement(Rectangle visibleRect,
4926                                          int orientation) {
4927        // Measure back from visible leading edge
4928        // If we hit the cell on its leading edge, it becomes the leading cell.
4929        // Else, use following cell
4930
4931        int row;
4932        int col;
4933
4934        int   newEdge;
4935        Point newCellLoc;
4936
4937        int visibleLeadingEdge = leadingEdge(visibleRect, orientation);
4938        boolean leftToRight = getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight();
4939        int newLeadingEdge;
4940
4941        // Roughly determine the new leading edge by measuring back from the
4942        // leading visible edge by the size of the visible rect, and find the
4943        // cell there.
4944        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL) {
4945            newEdge = visibleLeadingEdge - visibleRect.height;
4946            int x = visibleRect.x + (leftToRight ? 0 : visibleRect.width);
4947            newCellLoc = new Point(x, newEdge);
4948        }
4949        else if (leftToRight) {
4950            newEdge = visibleLeadingEdge - visibleRect.width;
4951            newCellLoc = new Point(newEdge, visibleRect.y);
4952        }
4953        else { // Horizontal, right-to-left
4954            newEdge = visibleLeadingEdge + visibleRect.width;
4955            newCellLoc = new Point(newEdge - 1, visibleRect.y);
4956        }
4957        row = rowAtPoint(newCellLoc);
4958        col = columnAtPoint(newCellLoc);
4959
4960        // If we're measuring past the beginning of the table, we get an invalid
4961        // cell.  Just go to the beginning of the table in this case.
4962        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL & row < 0) {
4963            newLeadingEdge = 0;
4964        }
4965        else if (orientation == SwingConstants.HORIZONTAL & col < 0) {
4966            if (leftToRight) {
4967                newLeadingEdge = 0;
4968            }
4969            else {
4970                newLeadingEdge = getWidth();
4971            }
4972        }
4973        else {
4974            // Refine our measurement
4975            Rectangle newCellRect = getCellRect(row, col, true);
4976            int newCellLeadingEdge = leadingEdge(newCellRect, orientation);
4977            int newCellTrailingEdge = trailingEdge(newCellRect, orientation);
4978
4979            // Usually, we hit in the middle of newCell, and want to scroll to
4980            // the beginning of the cell after newCell.  But there are a
4981            // couple corner cases where we want to scroll to the beginning of
4982            // newCell itself.  These cases are:
4983            // 1) newCell is so large that it ends at or extends into the
4984            //    visibleRect (newCell is the leading cell, or is adjacent to
4985            //    the leading cell)
4986            // 2) newEdge happens to fall right on the beginning of a cell
4987
4988            // Case 1
4989            if ((orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL || leftToRight) &&
4990                (newCellTrailingEdge >= visibleLeadingEdge)) {
4991                newLeadingEdge = newCellLeadingEdge;
4992            }
4993            else if (orientation == SwingConstants.HORIZONTAL &&
4994                     !leftToRight &&
4995                     newCellTrailingEdge <= visibleLeadingEdge) {
4996                newLeadingEdge = newCellLeadingEdge;
4997            }
4998            // Case 2:
4999            else if (newEdge == newCellLeadingEdge) {
5000                newLeadingEdge = newCellLeadingEdge;
5001            }
5002            // Common case: scroll to cell after newCell
5003            else {
5004                newLeadingEdge = newCellTrailingEdge;
5005            }
5006        }
5007        return Math.abs(visibleLeadingEdge - newLeadingEdge);
5008    }
5009
5010    /**
5011     * Called to get the block increment for downward scrolling in cases of
5012     * horizontal scrolling, or for vertical scrolling of a table with
5013     * variable row heights.
5014     */
5015    private int getNextBlockIncrement(Rectangle visibleRect,
5016                                      int orientation) {
5017        // Find the cell at the trailing edge.  Return the distance to put
5018        // that cell at the leading edge.
5019        int trailingRow = getTrailingRow(visibleRect);
5020        int trailingCol = getTrailingCol(visibleRect);
5021
5022        Rectangle cellRect;
5023        boolean cellFillsVis;
5024
5025        int cellLeadingEdge;
5026        int cellTrailingEdge;
5027        int newLeadingEdge;
5028        int visibleLeadingEdge = leadingEdge(visibleRect, orientation);
5029
5030        // If we couldn't find trailing cell, just return the size of the
5031        // visibleRect.  Note that, for instance, we don't need the
5032        // trailingCol to proceed if we're scrolling vertically, because
5033        // cellRect will still fill in the required dimensions.  This would
5034        // happen if we're scrolling vertically, and the table is not wide
5035        // enough to fill the visibleRect.
5036        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL && trailingRow < 0) {
5037            return visibleRect.height;
5038        }
5039        else if (orientation == SwingConstants.HORIZONTAL && trailingCol < 0) {
5040            return visibleRect.width;
5041        }
5042        cellRect = getCellRect(trailingRow, trailingCol, true);
5043        cellLeadingEdge = leadingEdge(cellRect, orientation);
5044        cellTrailingEdge = trailingEdge(cellRect, orientation);
5045
5046        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL ||
5047            getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight()) {
5048            cellFillsVis = cellLeadingEdge <= visibleLeadingEdge;
5049        }
5050        else { // Horizontal, right-to-left
5051            cellFillsVis = cellLeadingEdge >= visibleLeadingEdge;
5052        }
5053
5054        if (cellFillsVis) {
5055            // The visibleRect contains a single large cell.  Scroll to the end
5056            // of this cell, so the following cell is the first cell.
5057            newLeadingEdge = cellTrailingEdge;
5058        }
5059        else if (cellTrailingEdge == trailingEdge(visibleRect, orientation)) {
5060            // The trailing cell happens to end right at the end of the
5061            // visibleRect.  Again, scroll to the beginning of the next cell.
5062            newLeadingEdge = cellTrailingEdge;
5063        }
5064        else {
5065            // Common case: the trailing cell is partially visible, and isn't
5066            // big enough to take up the entire visibleRect.  Scroll so it
5067            // becomes the leading cell.
5068            newLeadingEdge = cellLeadingEdge;
5069        }
5070        return Math.abs(newLeadingEdge - visibleLeadingEdge);
5071    }
5072
5073    /*
5074     * Return the row at the top of the visibleRect
5075     *
5076     * May return -1
5077     */
5078    private int getLeadingRow(Rectangle visibleRect) {
5079        Point leadingPoint;
5080
5081        if (getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight()) {
5082            leadingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x, visibleRect.y);
5083        }
5084        else {
5085            leadingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x + visibleRect.width - 1,
5086                                     visibleRect.y);
5087        }
5088        return rowAtPoint(leadingPoint);
5089    }
5090
5091    /*
5092     * Return the column at the leading edge of the visibleRect.
5093     *
5094     * May return -1
5095     */
5096    private int getLeadingCol(Rectangle visibleRect) {
5097        Point leadingPoint;
5098
5099        if (getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight()) {
5100            leadingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x, visibleRect.y);
5101        }
5102        else {
5103            leadingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x + visibleRect.width - 1,
5104                                     visibleRect.y);
5105        }
5106        return columnAtPoint(leadingPoint);
5107    }
5108
5109    /*
5110     * Return the row at the bottom of the visibleRect.
5111     *
5112     * May return -1
5113     */
5114    private int getTrailingRow(Rectangle visibleRect) {
5115        Point trailingPoint;
5116
5117        if (getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight()) {
5118            trailingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x,
5119                                      visibleRect.y + visibleRect.height - 1);
5120        }
5121        else {
5122            trailingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x + visibleRect.width - 1,
5123                                      visibleRect.y + visibleRect.height - 1);
5124        }
5125        return rowAtPoint(trailingPoint);
5126    }
5127
5128    /*
5129     * Return the column at the trailing edge of the visibleRect.
5130     *
5131     * May return -1
5132     */
5133    private int getTrailingCol(Rectangle visibleRect) {
5134        Point trailingPoint;
5135
5136        if (getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight()) {
5137            trailingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x + visibleRect.width - 1,
5138                                      visibleRect.y);
5139        }
5140        else {
5141            trailingPoint = new Point(visibleRect.x, visibleRect.y);
5142        }
5143        return columnAtPoint(trailingPoint);
5144    }
5145
5146    /*
5147     * Returns the leading edge ("beginning") of the given Rectangle.
5148     * For VERTICAL, this is the top, for left-to-right, the left side, and for
5149     * right-to-left, the right side.
5150     */
5151    private int leadingEdge(Rectangle rect, int orientation) {
5152        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL) {
5153            return rect.y;
5154        }
5155        else if (getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight()) {
5156            return rect.x;
5157        }
5158        else { // Horizontal, right-to-left
5159            return rect.x + rect.width;
5160        }
5161    }
5162
5163    /*
5164     * Returns the trailing edge ("end") of the given Rectangle.
5165     * For VERTICAL, this is the bottom, for left-to-right, the right side, and
5166     * for right-to-left, the left side.
5167     */
5168    private int trailingEdge(Rectangle rect, int orientation) {
5169        if (orientation == SwingConstants.VERTICAL) {
5170            return rect.y + rect.height;
5171        }
5172        else if (getComponentOrientation().isLeftToRight()) {
5173            return rect.x + rect.width;
5174        }
5175        else { // Horizontal, right-to-left
5176            return rect.x;
5177        }
5178    }
5179
5180    /**
5181     * Returns false if <code>autoResizeMode</code> is set to
5182     * <code>AUTO_RESIZE_OFF</code>, which indicates that the
5183     * width of the viewport does not determine the width
5184     * of the table.  Otherwise returns true.
5185     *
5186     * @return false if <code>autoResizeMode</code> is set
5187     *   to <code>AUTO_RESIZE_OFF</code>, otherwise returns true
5188     * @see Scrollable#getScrollableTracksViewportWidth
5189     */
5190    public boolean getScrollableTracksViewportWidth() {
5191        return !(autoResizeMode == AUTO_RESIZE_OFF);
5192    }
5193
5194    /**
5195     * Returns {@code false} to indicate that the height of the viewport does
5196     * not determine the height of the table, unless
5197     * {@code getFillsViewportHeight} is {@code true} and the preferred height
5198     * of the table is smaller than the viewport's height.
5199     *
5200     * @return {@code false} unless {@code getFillsViewportHeight} is
5201     *         {@code true} and the table needs to be stretched to fill
5202     *         the viewport
5203     * @see Scrollable#getScrollableTracksViewportHeight
5204     * @see #setFillsViewportHeight
5205     * @see #getFillsViewportHeight
5206     */
5207    public boolean getScrollableTracksViewportHeight() {
5208        Container parent = SwingUtilities.getUnwrappedParent(this);
5209        return getFillsViewportHeight()
5210               && parent instanceof JViewport
5211               && parent.getHeight() > getPreferredSize().height;
5212    }
5213
5214    /**
5215     * Sets whether or not this table is always made large enough
5216     * to fill the height of an enclosing viewport. If the preferred
5217     * height of the table is smaller than the viewport, then the table
5218     * will be stretched to fill the viewport. In other words, this
5219     * ensures the table is never smaller than the viewport.
5220     * The default for this property is {@code false}.
5221     *
5222     * @param fillsViewportHeight whether or not this table is always
5223     *        made large enough to fill the height of an enclosing
5224     *        viewport
5225     * @see #getFillsViewportHeight
5226     * @see #getScrollableTracksViewportHeight
5227     * @since 1.6
5228     * @beaninfo
5229     *      bound: true
5230     *      description: Whether or not this table is always made large enough
5231     *                   to fill the height of an enclosing viewport
5232     */
5233    public void setFillsViewportHeight(boolean fillsViewportHeight) {
5234        boolean old = this.fillsViewportHeight;
5235        this.fillsViewportHeight = fillsViewportHeight;
5236        resizeAndRepaint();
5237        firePropertyChange("fillsViewportHeight", old, fillsViewportHeight);
5238    }
5239
5240    /**
5241     * Returns whether or not this table is always made large enough
5242     * to fill the height of an enclosing viewport.
5243     *
5244     * @return whether or not this table is always made large enough
5245     *         to fill the height of an enclosing viewport
5246     * @see #setFillsViewportHeight
5247     * @since 1.6
5248     */
5249    public boolean getFillsViewportHeight() {
5250        return fillsViewportHeight;
5251    }
5252
5253//
5254// Protected Methods
5255//
5256
5257    protected boolean processKeyBinding(KeyStroke ks, KeyEvent e,
5258                                        int condition, boolean pressed) {
5259        boolean retValue = super.processKeyBinding(ks, e, condition, pressed);
5260
5261        // Start editing when a key is typed. UI classes can disable this behavior
5262        // by setting the client property JTable.autoStartsEdit to Boolean.FALSE.
5263        if (!retValue && condition == WHEN_ANCESTOR_OF_FOCUSED_COMPONENT &&
5264            isFocusOwner() &&
5265            !Boolean.FALSE.equals(getClientProperty("JTable.autoStartsEdit"))) {
5266            // We do not have a binding for the event.
5267            Component editorComponent = getEditorComponent();
5268            if (editorComponent == null) {
5269                // Only attempt to install the editor on a KEY_PRESSED,
5270                if (e == null || e.getID() != KeyEvent.KEY_PRESSED) {
5271                    return false;
5272                }
5273                // Don't start when just a modifier is pressed
5274                int code = e.getKeyCode();
5275                if (code == KeyEvent.VK_SHIFT || code == KeyEvent.VK_CONTROL ||
5276                    code == KeyEvent.VK_ALT) {
5277                    return false;
5278                }
5279                // Try to install the editor
5280                int leadRow = getSelectionModel().getLeadSelectionIndex();
5281                int leadColumn = getColumnModel().getSelectionModel().
5282                                   getLeadSelectionIndex();
5283                if (leadRow != -1 && leadColumn != -1 && !isEditing()) {
5284                    if (!editCellAt(leadRow, leadColumn, e)) {
5285                        return false;
5286                    }
5287                }
5288                editorComponent = getEditorComponent();
5289                if (editorComponent == null) {
5290                    return false;
5291                }
5292            }
5293            // If the editorComponent is a JComponent, pass the event to it.
5294            if (editorComponent instanceof JComponent) {
5295                retValue = ((JComponent)editorComponent).processKeyBinding
5296                                        (ks, e, WHEN_FOCUSED, pressed);
5297                // If we have started an editor as a result of the user
5298                // pressing a key and the surrendersFocusOnKeystroke property
5299                // is true, give the focus to the new editor.
5300                if (getSurrendersFocusOnKeystroke()) {
5301                    editorComponent.requestFocus();
5302                }
5303            }
5304        }
5305        return retValue;
5306    }
5307
5308    private void setLazyValue(Hashtable h, Class c, String s) {
5309        h.put(c, new SwingLazyValue(s));
5310    }
5311
5312    private void setLazyRenderer(Class c, String s) {
5313        setLazyValue(defaultRenderersByColumnClass, c, s);
5314    }

5318     * booleans, and icons.
5319     * @see javax.swing.table.DefaultTableCellRenderer
5320     *
5321     */
5322    protected void createDefaultRenderers() {
5323        defaultRenderersByColumnClass = new UIDefaults(8, 0.75f);

5326        setLazyRenderer(Object.class, "javax.swing.table.DefaultTableCellRenderer$UIResource");
5327
5328        // Numbers
5329        setLazyRenderer(Number.class, "javax.swing.JTable$NumberRenderer");
5330
5331        // Doubles and Floats
5332        setLazyRenderer(Float.class, "javax.swing.JTable$DoubleRenderer");
5333        setLazyRenderer(Double.class, "javax.swing.JTable$DoubleRenderer");
5334
5335        // Dates
5336        setLazyRenderer(Date.class, "javax.swing.JTable$DateRenderer");
5337
5338        // Icons and ImageIcons
5339        setLazyRenderer(Icon.class, "javax.swing.JTable$IconRenderer");
5340        setLazyRenderer(ImageIcon.class, "javax.swing.JTable$IconRenderer");
5341
5342        // Booleans
5343        setLazyRenderer(Boolean.class, "javax.swing.JTable$BooleanRenderer");
5344    }

5399        public Component getTableCellRendererComponent(JTable table, Object value,
5400                                                       boolean isSelected, boolean hasFocus, int row, int column) {
5401            if (isSelected) {
5402                setForeground(table.getSelectionForeground());
5403                super.setBackground(table.getSelectionBackground());
5404            }
5405            else {
5406                setForeground(table.getForeground());
5407                setBackground(table.getBackground());
5408            }
5409            setSelected((value != null && ((Boolean)value).booleanValue()));
5410
5411            if (hasFocus) {
5412                setBorder(UIManager.getBorder("Table.focusCellHighlightBorder"));
5413            } else {
5414                setBorder(noFocusBorder);
5415            }
5416
5417            return this;

5442    /**
5443     * Default Editors
5444     */
5445    static class GenericEditor extends DefaultCellEditor {
5446
5447        Class[] argTypes = new Class[]{String.class};
5448        java.lang.reflect.Constructor constructor;
5449        Object value;
5450
5451        public GenericEditor() {
5452            super(new JTextField());
5453            getComponent().setName("Table.editor");
5454        }
5455
5456        public boolean stopCellEditing() {
5457            String s = (String)super.getCellEditorValue();
5458            // Here we are dealing with the case where a user
5459            // has deleted the string value in a cell, possibly
5460            // after a failed validation. Return null, so that
5461            // they have the option to replace the value with
5462            // null or use escape to restore the original.
5463            // For Strings, return "" for backward compatibility.
5464
5465            try {
5466                if ("".equals(s)) {
5467                    if (constructor.getDeclaringClass() == String.class) {
5468                        value = s;
5469                    }
5470                    return super.stopCellEditing();
5471                }
5472
5473                SwingUtilities2.checkAccess(constructor.getModifiers());
5474                value = constructor.newInstance(new Object[]{s});
5475            }
5476            catch (Exception e) {
5477                ((JComponent)getComponent()).setBorder(new LineBorder(Color.red));
5478                return false;
5479            }
5480            return super.stopCellEditing();
5481        }
5482
5483        public Component getTableCellEditorComponent(JTable table, Object value,
5484                                                 boolean isSelected,
5485                                                 int row, int column) {
5486            this.value = null;
5487            ((JComponent)getComponent()).setBorder(new LineBorder(Color.black));
5488            try {
5489                Class<?> type = table.getColumnClass(column);
5490                // Since our obligation is to produce a value which is
5491                // assignable for the required type it is OK to use the
5492                // String constructor for columns which are declared
5493                // to contain Objects. A String is an Object.
5494                if (type == Object.class) {
5495                    type = String.class;
5496                }
5497                ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(type);
5498                SwingUtilities2.checkAccess(type.getModifiers());
5499                constructor = type.getConstructor(argTypes);
5500            }
5501            catch (Exception e) {
5502                return null;
5503            }
5504            return super.getTableCellEditorComponent(table, value, isSelected, row, column);
5505        }
5506
5507        public Object getCellEditorValue() {
5508            return value;
5509        }
5510    }

5513
5514        public NumberEditor() {
5515            ((JTextField)getComponent()).setHorizontalAlignment(JTextField.RIGHT);
5516        }
5517    }

5537

5543        setRowSelectionAllowed(true);

5546        setEditingRow(-1);
5547        setSurrendersFocusOnKeystroke(false);
5548        setPreferredScrollableViewportSize(new Dimension(450, 400));
5549
5550        // I'm registered to do tool tips so we can draw tips for the renderers
5551        ToolTipManager toolTipManager = ToolTipManager.sharedInstance();

5661    /**
5662     * Returns an appropriate renderer for the cell specified by this row and
5663     * column. If the <code>TableColumn</code> for this column has a non-null
5664     * renderer, returns that.  If not, finds the class of the data in
5665     * this column (using <code>getColumnClass</code>)
5666     * and returns the default renderer for this type of data.
5667     * <p>
5668     * <b>Note:</b>
5669     * Throughout the table package, the internal implementations always
5670     * use this method to provide renderers so that this default behavior
5671     * can be safely overridden by a subclass.
5672     *
5673     * @param row       the row of the cell to render, where 0 is the first row
5674     * @param column    the column of the cell to render,
5675     *                  where 0 is the first column
5676     * @return the assigned renderer; if <code>null</code>
5677     *                  returns the default renderer
5678     *                  for this type of object
5679     * @see javax.swing.table.DefaultTableCellRenderer
5680     * @see javax.swing.table.TableColumn#setCellRenderer
5681     * @see #setDefaultRenderer
5682     */
5683    public TableCellRenderer getCellRenderer(int row, int column) {
5684        TableColumn tableColumn = getColumnModel().getColumn(column);
5685        TableCellRenderer renderer = tableColumn.getCellRenderer();
5686        if (renderer == null) {
5687            renderer = getDefaultRenderer(getColumnClass(column));
5688        }
5689        return renderer;
5690    }
5691
5692    /**
5693     * Prepares the renderer by querying the data model for the
5694     * value and selection state
5695     * of the cell at <code>row</code>, <code>column</code>.
5696     * Returns the component (may be a <code>Component</code>
5697     * or a <code>JComponent</code>) under the event location.
5698     * <p>
5699     * During a printing operation, this method will configure the
5700     * renderer without indicating selection or focus, to prevent
5701     * them from appearing in the printed output. To do other
5702     * customizations based on whether or not the table is being
5703     * printed, you can check the value of
5704     * {@link javax.swing.JComponent#isPaintingForPrint()}, either here
5705     * or within custom renderers.
5706     * <p>
5707     * <b>Note:</b>
5708     * Throughout the table package, the internal implementations always
5709     * use this method to prepare renderers so that this default behavior
5710     * can be safely overridden by a subclass.
5711     *
5712     * @param renderer  the <code>TableCellRenderer</code> to prepare
5713     * @param row       the row of the cell to render, where 0 is the first row
5714     * @param column    the column of the cell to render,
5715     *                  where 0 is the first column
5716     * @return          the <code>Component</code> under the event location
5717     */
5718    public Component prepareRenderer(TableCellRenderer renderer, int row, int column) {
5719        Object value = getValueAt(row, column);
5720
5721        boolean isSelected = false;
5722        boolean hasFocus = false;
5723
5724        // Only indicate the selection and focused cell if not printing
5725        if (!isPaintingForPrint()) {
5726            isSelected = isCellSelected(row, column);
5727
5728            boolean rowIsLead =
5729                (selectionModel.getLeadSelectionIndex() == row);
5730            boolean colIsLead =
5731                (columnModel.getSelectionModel().getLeadSelectionIndex() == column);
5732
5733            hasFocus = (rowIsLead && colIsLead) && isFocusOwner();
5734        }
5735
5736        return renderer.getTableCellRendererComponent(this, value,
5737                                                      isSelected, hasFocus,
5738                                                      row, column);
5739    }
5740
5741    /**
5742     * Returns an appropriate editor for the cell specified by
5743     * <code>row</code> and <code>column</code>. If the
5744     * <code>TableColumn</code> for this column has a non-null editor,
5745     * returns that.  If not, finds the class of the data in this
5746     * column (using <code>getColumnClass</code>)
5747     * and returns the default editor for this type of data.
5748     * <p>
5749     * <b>Note:</b>
5750     * Throughout the table package, the internal implementations always
5751     * use this method to provide editors so that this default behavior
5752     * can be safely overridden by a subclass.
5753     *
5754     * @param row       the row of the cell to edit, where 0 is the first row
5755     * @param column    the column of the cell to edit,
5756     *                  where 0 is the first column
5757     * @return          the editor for this cell;
5758     *                  if <code>null</code> return the default editor for
5759     *                  this type of cell
5760     * @see DefaultCellEditor
5761     */
5762    public TableCellEditor getCellEditor(int row, int column) {
5763        TableColumn tableColumn = getColumnModel().getColumn(column);
5764        TableCellEditor editor = tableColumn.getCellEditor();
5765        if (editor == null) {
5766            editor = getDefaultEditor(getColumnClass(column));
5767        }
5768        return editor;
5769    }
5770
5771
5772    /**
5773     * Prepares the editor by querying the data model for the value and
5774     * selection state of the cell at <code>row</code>, <code>column</code>.
5775     * <p>
5776     * <b>Note:</b>
5777     * Throughout the table package, the internal implementations always
5778     * use this method to prepare editors so that this default behavior
5779     * can be safely overridden by a subclass.
5780     *
5781     * @param editor  the <code>TableCellEditor</code> to set up
5782     * @param row     the row of the cell to edit,
5783     *                where 0 is the first row
5784     * @param column  the column of the cell to edit,
5785     *                where 0 is the first column
5786     * @return the <code>Component</code> being edited
5787     */
5788    public Component prepareEditor(TableCellEditor editor, int row, int column) {
5789        Object value = getValueAt(row, column);
5790        boolean isSelected = isCellSelected(row, column);
5791        Component comp = editor.getTableCellEditorComponent(this, value, isSelected,
5792                                                  row, column);
5793        if (comp instanceof JComponent) {
5794            JComponent jComp = (JComponent)comp;
5795            if (jComp.getNextFocusableComponent() == null) {
5796                jComp.setNextFocusableComponent(this);
5797            }
5798        }
5799        return comp;
5800    }
5801
5802    /**
5803     * Discards the editor object and frees the real estate it used for
5804     * cell rendering.
5805     */
5806    public void removeEditor() {
5807        KeyboardFocusManager.getCurrentKeyboardFocusManager().
5808            removePropertyChangeListener("permanentFocusOwner", editorRemover);
5809        editorRemover = null;
5810
5811        TableCellEditor editor = getCellEditor();
5812        if(editor != null) {
5813            editor.removeCellEditorListener(this);
5814            if (editorComp != null) {
5815                Component focusOwner =
5816                        KeyboardFocusManager.getCurrentKeyboardFocusManager().getFocusOwner();
5817                boolean isFocusOwnerInTheTable = focusOwner != null?
5818                        SwingUtilities.isDescendingFrom(focusOwner, this):false;
5819                remove(editorComp);
5820                if(isFocusOwnerInTheTable) {
5821                    requestFocusInWindow();
5822                }
5823            }
5824
5825            Rectangle cellRect = getCellRect(editingRow, editingColumn, false);
5826
5827            setCellEditor(null);
5828            setEditingColumn(-1);
5829            setEditingRow(-1);
5830            editorComp = null;
5831
5832            repaint(cellRect);
5833        }
5834    }
5835
5836//
5837// Serialization
5838//
5839
5840    /**
5841     * See readObject() and writeObject() in JComponent for more
5842     * information about serialization in Swing.
5843     */
5844    private void writeObject(ObjectOutputStream s) throws IOException {
5845        s.defaultWriteObject();
5846        if (getUIClassID().equals(uiClassID)) {
5847            byte count = JComponent.getWriteObjCounter(this);
5848            JComponent.setWriteObjCounter(this, --count);
5849            if (count == 0 && ui != null) {
5850                ui.installUI(this);
5851            }
5852        }
5853    }
5854
5855    private void readObject(ObjectInputStream s)
5856        throws IOException, ClassNotFoundException
5857    {
5858        s.defaultReadObject();
5859        if ((ui != null) && (getUIClassID().equals(uiClassID))) {
5860            ui.installUI(this);
5861        }
5862        createDefaultRenderers();
5863        createDefaultEditors();
5864
5865        // If ToolTipText != null, then the tooltip has already been
5866        // registered by JComponent.readObject() and we don't want
5867        // to re-register here
5868        if (getToolTipText() == null) {
5869            ToolTipManager.sharedInstance().registerComponent(this);
5870         }
5871    }
5872
5873    /* Called from the JComponent's EnableSerializationFocusListener to
5874     * do any Swing-specific pre-serialization configuration.
5875     */
5876    void compWriteObjectNotify() {
5877        super.compWriteObjectNotify();
5878        // If ToolTipText != null, then the tooltip has already been
5879        // unregistered by JComponent.compWriteObjectNotify()
5880        if (getToolTipText() == null) {
5881            ToolTipManager.sharedInstance().unregisterComponent(this);
5882        }
5883    }

5885    /**
5886     * Returns a string representation of this table. This method
5887     * is intended to be used only for debugging purposes, and the
5888     * content and format of the returned string may vary between
5889     * implementations. The returned string may be empty but may not
5890     * be <code>null</code>.
5891     *
5892     * @return  a string representation of this table
5893     */
5894    protected String paramString() {
5895        String gridColorString = (gridColor != null ?
5896                                  gridColor.toString() : "");
5897        String showHorizontalLinesString = (showHorizontalLines ?
5898                                            "true" : "false");
5899        String showVerticalLinesString = (showVerticalLines ?
5900                                          "true" : "false");
5901        String autoResizeModeString;
5902        if (autoResizeMode == AUTO_RESIZE_OFF) {
5903            autoResizeModeString = "AUTO_RESIZE_OFF";
5904        } else if (autoResizeMode == AUTO_RESIZE_NEXT_COLUMN) {
5905            autoResizeModeString = "AUTO_RESIZE_NEXT_COLUMN";
5906        } else if (autoResizeMode == AUTO_RESIZE_SUBSEQUENT_COLUMNS) {
5907            autoResizeModeString = "AUTO_RESIZE_SUBSEQUENT_COLUMNS";
5908        } else if (autoResizeMode == AUTO_RESIZE_LAST_COLUMN) {
5909            autoResizeModeString = "AUTO_RESIZE_LAST_COLUMN";
5910        } else if (autoResizeMode == AUTO_RESIZE_ALL_COLUMNS)  {
5911            autoResizeModeString = "AUTO_RESIZE_ALL_COLUMNS";
5912        } else autoResizeModeString = "";
5913        String autoCreateColumnsFromModelString = (autoCreateColumnsFromModel ?
5914                                                   "true" : "false");
5915        String preferredViewportSizeString = (preferredViewportSize != null ?
5916                                              preferredViewportSize.toString()
5917                                              : "");
5918        String rowSelectionAllowedString = (rowSelectionAllowed ?
5919                                            "true" : "false");
5920        String cellSelectionEnabledString = (cellSelectionEnabled ?
5921                                            "true" : "false");
5922        String selectionForegroundString = (selectionForeground != null ?
5923                                            selectionForeground.toString() :
5924                                            "");
5925        String selectionBackgroundString = (selectionBackground != null ?
5926                                            selectionBackground.toString() :
5927                                            "");
5928
5929        return super.paramString() +
5930        ",autoCreateColumnsFromModel=" + autoCreateColumnsFromModelString +
5931        ",autoResizeMode=" + autoResizeModeString +
5932        ",cellSelectionEnabled=" + cellSelectionEnabledString +
5933        ",editingColumn=" + editingColumn +
5934        ",editingRow=" + editingRow +
5935        ",gridColor=" + gridColorString +
5936        ",preferredViewportSize=" + preferredViewportSizeString +
5937        ",rowHeight=" + rowHeight +
5938        ",rowMargin=" + rowMargin +
5939        ",rowSelectionAllowed=" + rowSelectionAllowedString +
5940        ",selectionBackground=" + selectionBackgroundString +
5941        ",selectionForeground=" + selectionForegroundString +
5942        ",showHorizontalLines=" + showHorizontalLinesString +
5943        ",showVerticalLines=" + showVerticalLinesString;
5944    }
5945
5946    // This class tracks changes in the keyboard focus state. It is used
5947    // when the JTable is editing to determine when to cancel the edit.
5948    // If focus switches to a component outside of the jtable, but in the
5949    // same window, this will cancel editing.
5950    class CellEditorRemover implements PropertyChangeListener {
5951        KeyboardFocusManager focusManager;
5952
5953        public CellEditorRemover(KeyboardFocusManager fm) {
5954            this.focusManager = fm;
5955        }
5956
5957        public void propertyChange(PropertyChangeEvent ev) {
5958            if (!isEditing() || getClientProperty("terminateEditOnFocusLost") != Boolean.TRUE) {
5959                return;
5960            }
5961
5962            Component c = focusManager.getPermanentFocusOwner();
5963            while (c != null) {
5964                if (c == JTable.this) {
5965                    // focus remains inside the table
5966                    return;
5967                } else if ((c instanceof Window) ||
5968                           (c instanceof Applet && c.getParent() == null)) {
5969                    if (c == SwingUtilities.getRoot(JTable.this)) {
5970                        if (!getCellEditor().stopCellEditing()) {
5971                            getCellEditor().cancelCellEditing();
5972                        }
5973                    }
5974                    break;
5975                }
5976                c = c.getParent();
5977            }
5978        }
5979    }

6121
6122    /**
6123     * Prints this <code>JTable</code>. Takes steps that the majority of
6124     * developers would take in order to print a <code>JTable</code>.
6125     * In short, it prepares the table, calls <code>getPrintable</code> to
6126     * fetch an appropriate <code>Printable</code>, and then sends it to the
6127     * printer.
6128     * <p>
6129     * A <code>boolean</code> parameter allows you to specify whether or not
6130     * a printing dialog is displayed to the user. When it is, the user may
6131     * use the dialog to change the destination printer or printing attributes,
6132     * or even to cancel the print. Another two parameters allow for a
6133     * <code>PrintService</code> and printing attributes to be specified.
6134     * These parameters can be used either to provide initial values for the
6135     * print dialog, or to specify values when the dialog is not shown.
6136     * <p>
6137     * A second <code>boolean</code> parameter allows you to specify whether
6138     * or not to perform printing in an interactive mode. If <code>true</code>,
6139     * a modal progress dialog, with an abort option, is displayed for the
6140     * duration of printing . This dialog also prevents any user action which
6141     * may affect the table. However, it can not prevent the table from being
6142     * modified by code (for example, another thread that posts updates using
6143     * <code>SwingUtilities.invokeLater</code>). It is therefore the
6144     * responsibility of the developer to ensure that no other code modifies
6145     * the table in any way during printing (invalid modifications include
6146     * changes in: size, renderers, or underlying data). Printing behavior is
6147     * undefined when the table is changed during printing.
6148     * <p>
6149     * If <code>false</code> is specified for this parameter, no dialog will
6150     * be displayed and printing will begin immediately on the event-dispatch
6151     * thread. This blocks any other events, including repaints, from being
6152     * processed until printing is complete. Although this effectively prevents
6153     * the table from being changed, it doesn't provide a good user experience.
6154     * For this reason, specifying <code>false</code> is only recommended when
6155     * printing from an application with no visible GUI.
6156     * <p>
6157     * Note: Attempting to show the printing dialog or run interactively, while
6158     * in headless mode, will result in a <code>HeadlessException</code>.
6159     * <p>
6160     * Before fetching the printable, this method will gracefully terminate
6161     * editing, if necessary, to prevent an editor from showing in the printed
6162     * result. Additionally, <code>JTable</code> will prepare its renderers
6163     * during printing such that selection and focus are not indicated.
6164     * As far as customizing further how the table looks in the printout,
6165     * developers can provide custom renderers or paint code that conditionalize
6166     * on the value of {@link javax.swing.JComponent#isPaintingForPrint()}.
6167     * <p>
6168     * See {@link #getPrintable} for more description on how the table is
6169     * printed.
6170     *
6171     * @param  printMode        the printing mode that the printable should use
6172     * @param  headerFormat     a <code>MessageFormat</code> specifying the text
6173     *                          to be used in printing a header,
6174     *                          or <code>null</code> for none
6175     * @param  footerFormat     a <code>MessageFormat</code> specifying the text
6176     *                          to be used in printing a footer,
6177     *                          or <code>null</code> for none
6178     * @param  showPrintDialog  whether or not to display a print dialog
6179     * @param  attr             a <code>PrintRequestAttributeSet</code>
6180     *                          specifying any printing attributes,
6181     *                          or <code>null</code> for none
6182     * @param  interactive      whether or not to print in an interactive mode
6183     * @param  service          the destination <code>PrintService</code>,
6184     *                          or <code>null</code> to use the default printer
6185     * @return true, unless printing is cancelled by the user
6186     * @throws HeadlessException if the method is asked to show a printing
6187     *                           dialog or run interactively, and
6188     *                           <code>GraphicsEnvironment.isHeadless</code>
6189     *                           returns <code>true</code>
6190     * @throws  SecurityException if a security manager exists and its
6191     *          {@link java.lang.SecurityManager#checkPrintJobAccess}
6192     *          method disallows this thread from creating a print job request
6193     * @throws PrinterException if an error in the print system causes the job
6194     *                          to be aborted
6195     * @see #getPrintable
6196     * @see java.awt.GraphicsEnvironment#isHeadless
6197     *
6198     * @since 1.6
6199     */
6200    public boolean print(PrintMode printMode,
6201                         MessageFormat headerFormat,
6202                         MessageFormat footerFormat,
6203                         boolean showPrintDialog,
6204                         PrintRequestAttributeSet attr,
6205                         boolean interactive,
6206                         PrintService service) throws PrinterException,
6207                                                      HeadlessException {
6208
6209        // complain early if an invalid parameter is specified for headless mode
6210        boolean isHeadless = GraphicsEnvironment.isHeadless();
6211        if (isHeadless) {
6212            if (showPrintDialog) {
6213                throw new HeadlessException("Can't show print dialog.");
6214            }
6215
6216            if (interactive) {
6217                throw new HeadlessException("Can't run interactively.");
6218            }
6219        }
6220
6221        // Get a PrinterJob.
6222        // Do this before anything with side-effects since it may throw a
6223        // security exception - in which case we don't want to do anything else.
6224        final PrinterJob job = PrinterJob.getPrinterJob();
6225
6226        if (isEditing()) {
6227            // try to stop cell editing, and failing that, cancel it
6228            if (!getCellEditor().stopCellEditing()) {
6229                getCellEditor().cancelCellEditing();
6230            }
6231        }
6232
6233        if (attr == null) {
6234            attr = new HashPrintRequestAttributeSet();
6235        }
6236
6237        final PrintingStatus printingStatus;
6238
6239         // fetch the Printable
6240        Printable printable =
6241             getPrintable(printMode, headerFormat, footerFormat);
6242
6243        if (interactive) {
6244            // wrap the Printable so that we can print on another thread
6245            printable = new ThreadSafePrintable(printable);
6246            printingStatus = PrintingStatus.createPrintingStatus(this, job);
6247            printable = printingStatus.createNotificationPrintable(printable);
6248        } else {
6249            // to please compiler
6250            printingStatus = null;
6251        }
6252
6253        // set the printable on the PrinterJob
6254        job.setPrintable(printable);
6255
6256        // if specified, set the PrintService on the PrinterJob
6257        if (service != null) {
6258            job.setPrintService(service);
6259        }
6260
6261        // if requested, show the print dialog
6262        if (showPrintDialog && !job.printDialog(attr)) {
6263            // the user cancelled the print dialog
6264            return false;
6265        }
6266
6267        // if not interactive, just print on this thread (no dialog)
6268        if (!interactive) {
6269            // do the printing
6270            job.print(attr);
6271
6272            // we're done
6273            return true;
6274        }
6275
6276        // make sure this is clear since we'll check it after
6277        printError = null;
6278
6279        // to synchronize on
6280        final Object lock = new Object();
6281
6282        // copied so we can access from the inner class
6283        final PrintRequestAttributeSet copyAttr = attr;
6284
6285        // this runnable will be used to do the printing
6286        // (and save any throwables) on another thread
6287        Runnable runnable = new Runnable() {
6288            public void run() {
6289                try {
6290                    // do the printing
6291                    job.print(copyAttr);
6292                } catch (Throwable t) {
6293                    // save any Throwable to be rethrown
6294                    synchronized(lock) {
6295                        printError = t;
6296                    }
6297                } finally {
6298                    // we're finished - hide the dialog
6299                    printingStatus.dispose();
6300                }
6301            }
6302        };
6303
6304        // start printing on another thread
6305        Thread th = new Thread(runnable);
6306        th.start();
6307
6308        printingStatus.showModal(true);
6309
6310        // look for any error that the printing may have generated
6311        Throwable pe;
6312        synchronized(lock) {
6313            pe = printError;
6314            printError = null;
6315        }
6316
6317        // check the type of error and handle it
6318        if (pe != null) {
6319            // a subclass of PrinterException meaning the job was aborted,
6320            // in this case, by the user
6321            if (pe instanceof PrinterAbortException) {
6322                return false;
6323            } else if (pe instanceof PrinterException) {
6324                throw (PrinterException)pe;
6325            } else if (pe instanceof RuntimeException) {
6326                throw (RuntimeException)pe;
6327            } else if (pe instanceof Error) {
6328                throw (Error)pe;
6329            }
6330
6331            // can not happen
6332            throw new AssertionError(pe);
6333        }
6334
6335        return true;
6336    }
6337
6338    /**
6339     * Return a <code>Printable</code> for use in printing this JTable.
6340     * <p>
6341     * This method is meant for those wishing to customize the default
6342     * <code>Printable</code> implementation used by <code>JTable</code>'s
6343     * <code>print</code> methods. Developers wanting simply to print the table
6344     * should use one of those methods directly.
6345     * <p>
6346     * The <code>Printable</code> can be requested in one of two printing modes.
6347     * In both modes, it spreads table rows naturally in sequence across
6348     * multiple pages, fitting as many rows as possible per page.
6349     * <code>PrintMode.NORMAL</code> specifies that the table be
6350     * printed at its current size. In this mode, there may be a need to spread
6351     * columns across pages in a similar manner to that of the rows. When the
6352     * need arises, columns are distributed in an order consistent with the
6353     * table's <code>ComponentOrientation</code>.
6354     * <code>PrintMode.FIT_WIDTH</code> specifies that the output be
6355     * scaled smaller, if necessary, to fit the table's entire width
6356     * (and thereby all columns) on each page. Width and height are scaled
6357     * equally, maintaining the aspect ratio of the output.
6358     * <p>
6359     * The <code>Printable</code> heads the portion of table on each page
6360     * with the appropriate section from the table's <code>JTableHeader</code>,
6361     * if it has one.
6362     * <p>
6363     * Header and footer text can be added to the output by providing
6364     * <code>MessageFormat</code> arguments. The printing code requests
6365     * Strings from the formats, providing a single item which may be included
6366     * in the formatted string: an <code>Integer</code> representing the current
6367     * page number.
6368     * <p>
6369     * You are encouraged to read the documentation for
6370     * <code>MessageFormat</code> as some characters, such as single-quote,
6371     * are special and need to be escaped.
6372     * <p>
6373     * Here's an example of creating a <code>MessageFormat</code> that can be
6374     * used to print "Duke's Table: Page - " and the current page number:
6375     * <p>
6376     * <pre>
6377     *     // notice the escaping of the single quote
6378     *     // notice how the page number is included with "{0}"
6379     *     MessageFormat format = new MessageFormat("Duke''s Table: Page - {0}");
6380     * </pre>
6381     * <p>
6382     * The <code>Printable</code> constrains what it draws to the printable
6383     * area of each page that it prints. Under certain circumstances, it may
6384     * find it impossible to fit all of a page's content into that area. In
6385     * these cases the output may be clipped, but the implementation
6386     * makes an effort to do something reasonable. Here are a few situations
6387     * where this is known to occur, and how they may be handled by this
6388     * particular implementation:
6389     * <ul>
6390     *   <li>In any mode, when the header or footer text is too wide to fit
6391     *       completely in the printable area -- print as much of the text as
6392     *       possible starting from the beginning, as determined by the table's
6393     *       <code>ComponentOrientation</code>.
6394     *   <li>In any mode, when a row is too tall to fit in the
6395     *       printable area -- print the upper-most portion of the row
6396     *       and paint no lower border on the table.
6397     *   <li>In <code>PrintMode.NORMAL</code> when a column
6398     *       is too wide to fit in the printable area -- print the center
6399     *       portion of the column and leave the left and right borders
6400     *       off the table.
6401     * </ul>
6402     * <p>
6403     * It is entirely valid for this <code>Printable</code> to be wrapped
6404     * inside another in order to create complex reports and documents. You may
6405     * even request that different pages be rendered into different sized
6406     * printable areas. The implementation must be prepared to handle this
6407     * (possibly by doing its layout calculations on the fly). However,
6408     * providing different heights to each page will likely not work well
6409     * with <code>PrintMode.NORMAL</code> when it has to spread columns
6410     * across pages.
6411     * <p>
6412     * As far as customizing how the table looks in the printed result,
6413     * <code>JTable</code> itself will take care of hiding the selection
6414     * and focus during printing. For additional customizations, your
6415     * renderers or painting code can customize the look based on the value
6416     * of {@link javax.swing.JComponent#isPaintingForPrint()}
6417     * <p>
6418     * Also, <i>before</i> calling this method you may wish to <i>first</i>
6419     * modify the state of the table, such as to cancel cell editing or
6420     * have the user size the table appropriately. However, you must not
6421     * modify the state of the table <i>after</i> this <code>Printable</code>
6422     * has been fetched (invalid modifications include changes in size or
6423     * underlying data). The behavior of the returned <code>Printable</code>
6424     * is undefined once the table has been changed.
6425     *
6426     * @param  printMode     the printing mode that the printable should use
6427     * @param  headerFormat  a <code>MessageFormat</code> specifying the text to
6428     *                       be used in printing a header, or null for none
6429     * @param  footerFormat  a <code>MessageFormat</code> specifying the text to
6430     *                       be used in printing a footer, or null for none
6431     * @return a <code>Printable</code> for printing this JTable
6432     * @see #print(JTable.PrintMode, MessageFormat, MessageFormat,
6433     *             boolean, PrintRequestAttributeSet, boolean)
6434     * @see Printable
6435     * @see PrinterJob
6436     *
6437     * @since 1.5
6438     */
6439    public Printable getPrintable(PrintMode printMode,
6440                                  MessageFormat headerFormat,
6441                                  MessageFormat footerFormat) {
6442
6443        return new TablePrintable(this, printMode, headerFormat, footerFormat);
6444    }
6445
6446
6447    /**
6448     * A <code>Printable</code> implementation that wraps another
6449     * <code>Printable</code>, making it safe for printing on another thread.
6450     */
6451    private class ThreadSafePrintable implements Printable {
6452
6453        /** The delegate <code>Printable</code>. */
6454        private Printable printDelegate;
6455
6456        /**
6457         * To communicate any return value when delegating.
6458         */
6459        private int retVal;
6460
6461        /**
6462         * To communicate any <code>Throwable</code> when delegating.
6463         */
6464        private Throwable retThrowable;
6465
6466        /**
6467         * Construct a <code>ThreadSafePrintable</code> around the given
6468         * delegate.
6469         *
6470         * @param printDelegate the <code>Printable</code> to delegate to
6471         */
6472        public ThreadSafePrintable(Printable printDelegate) {
6473            this.printDelegate = printDelegate;
6474        }
6475
6476        /**
6477         * Prints the specified page into the given {@link Graphics}
6478         * context, in the specified format.
6479         * <p>
6480         * Regardless of what thread this method is called on, all calls into
6481         * the delegate will be done on the event-dispatch thread.
6482         *
6483         * @param   graphics    the context into which the page is drawn
6484         * @param   pageFormat  the size and orientation of the page being drawn
6485         * @param   pageIndex   the zero based index of the page to be drawn
6486         * @return  PAGE_EXISTS if the page is rendered successfully, or
6487         *          NO_SUCH_PAGE if a non-existent page index is specified
6488         * @throws  PrinterException if an error causes printing to be aborted
6489         */
6490        public int print(final Graphics graphics,
6491                         final PageFormat pageFormat,
6492                         final int pageIndex) throws PrinterException {
6493
6494            // We'll use this Runnable
6495            Runnable runnable = new Runnable() {
6496                public synchronized void run() {
6497                    try {
6498                        // call into the delegate and save the return value
6499                        retVal = printDelegate.print(graphics, pageFormat, pageIndex);
6500                    } catch (Throwable throwable) {
6501                        // save any Throwable to be rethrown
6502                        retThrowable = throwable;
6503                    } finally {
6504                        // notify the caller that we're done
6505                        notifyAll();
6506                    }
6507                }
6508            };
6509
6510            synchronized(runnable) {
6511                // make sure these are initialized
6512                retVal = -1;
6513                retThrowable = null;
6514
6515                // call into the EDT
6516                SwingUtilities.invokeLater(runnable);
6517
6518                // wait for the runnable to finish
6519                while (retVal == -1 && retThrowable == null) {
6520                    try {
6521                        runnable.wait();
6522                    } catch (InterruptedException ie) {
6523                        // short process, safe to ignore interrupts
6524                    }
6525                }
6526
6527                // if the delegate threw a throwable, rethrow it here
6528                if (retThrowable != null) {
6529                    if (retThrowable instanceof PrinterException) {
6530                        throw (PrinterException)retThrowable;
6531                    } else if (retThrowable instanceof RuntimeException) {
6532                        throw (RuntimeException)retThrowable;
6533                    } else if (retThrowable instanceof Error) {
6534                        throw (Error)retThrowable;
6535                    }
6536
6537                    // can not happen
6538                    throw new AssertionError(retThrowable);
6539                }
6540
6541                return retVal;
6542            }
6543        }
6544    }
6545

6551    /**
6552     * Gets the AccessibleContext associated with this JTable.
6553     * For tables, the AccessibleContext takes the form of an
6554     * AccessibleJTable.
6555     * A new AccessibleJTable instance is created if necessary.
6556     *
6557     * @return an AccessibleJTable that serves as the
6558     *         AccessibleContext of this JTable
6559     */
6560    public AccessibleContext getAccessibleContext() {
6561        if (accessibleContext == null) {
6562            accessibleContext = new AccessibleJTable();
6563        }
6564        return accessibleContext;
6565    }

6567    //
6568    // *** should also implement AccessibleSelection?
6569    // *** and what's up with keyboard navigation/manipulation?
6570    //
6571    /**
6572     * This class implements accessibility support for the
6573     * <code>JTable</code> class.  It provides an implementation of the
6574     * Java Accessibility API appropriate to table user-interface elements.
6575     * <p>
6576     * <strong>Warning:</strong>
6577     * Serialized objects of this class will not be compatible with
6578     * future Swing releases. The current serialization support is
6579     * appropriate for short term storage or RMI between applications running
6580     * the same version of Swing.  As of 1.4, support for long term storage
6581     * of all JavaBeans<sup><font size="-2">TM</font></sup>
6582     * has been added to the <code>java.beans</code> package.
6583     * Please see {@link java.beans.XMLEncoder}.
6584     */
6585    protected class AccessibleJTable extends AccessibleJComponent
6586    implements AccessibleSelection, ListSelectionListener, TableModelListener,
6587    TableColumnModelListener, CellEditorListener, PropertyChangeListener,
6588    AccessibleExtendedTable {
6589
6590        int previousFocusedRow;
6591        int previousFocusedCol;
6592
6593        /**
6594         * AccessibleJTable constructor
6595         *
6596         * @since 1.5
6597         */
6598        protected AccessibleJTable() {
6599            super();
6600            JTable.this.addPropertyChangeListener(this);
6601            JTable.this.getSelectionModel().addListSelectionListener(this);
6602            TableColumnModel tcm = JTable.this.getColumnModel();
6603            tcm.addColumnModelListener(this);
6604            tcm.getSelectionModel().addListSelectionListener(this);
6605            JTable.this.getModel().addTableModelListener(this);
6606            previousFocusedRow = JTable.this.getSelectionModel().
6607                                        getLeadSelectionIndex();
6608            previousFocusedCol = JTable.this.getColumnModel().
6609                                        getSelectionModel().getLeadSelectionIndex();
6610        }
6611
6612    // Listeners to track model, etc. changes to as to re-place the other
6613    // listeners
6614
6615        /**
6616         * Track changes to selection model, column model, etc. so as to
6617         * be able to re-place listeners on those in order to pass on
6618         * information to the Accessibility PropertyChange mechanism
6619         */
6620        public void propertyChange(PropertyChangeEvent e) {
6621            String name = e.getPropertyName();
6622            Object oldValue = e.getOldValue();
6623            Object newValue = e.getNewValue();
6624
6625                // re-set tableModel listeners
6626            if (name.compareTo("model") == 0) {
6627
6628                if (oldValue != null && oldValue instanceof TableModel) {
6629                    ((TableModel) oldValue).removeTableModelListener(this);
6630                }
6631                if (newValue != null && newValue instanceof TableModel) {
6632                    ((TableModel) newValue).addTableModelListener(this);
6633                }
6634
6635                // re-set selectionModel listeners
6636            } else if (name.compareTo("selectionModel") == 0) {
6637
6638                Object source = e.getSource();
6639                if (source == JTable.this) {    // row selection model
6640
6641                    if (oldValue != null &&
6642                        oldValue instanceof ListSelectionModel) {
6643                        ((ListSelectionModel) oldValue).removeListSelectionListener(this);
6644                    }
6645                    if (newValue != null &&
6646                        newValue instanceof ListSelectionModel) {
6647                        ((ListSelectionModel) newValue).addListSelectionListener(this);
6648                    }
6649
6650                } else if (source == JTable.this.getColumnModel()) {
6651
6652                    if (oldValue != null &&
6653                        oldValue instanceof ListSelectionModel) {
6654                        ((ListSelectionModel) oldValue).removeListSelectionListener(this);
6655                    }
6656                    if (newValue != null &&
6657                        newValue instanceof ListSelectionModel) {
6658                        ((ListSelectionModel) newValue).addListSelectionListener(this);
6659                    }
6660
6661                } else {
6662                  //        System.out.println("!!! Bug in source of selectionModel propertyChangeEvent");
6663                }
6664
6665                // re-set columnModel listeners
6666                // and column's selection property listener as well
6667            } else if (name.compareTo("columnModel") == 0) {
6668
6669                if (oldValue != null && oldValue instanceof TableColumnModel) {
6670                    TableColumnModel tcm = (TableColumnModel) oldValue;
6671                    tcm.removeColumnModelListener(this);
6672                    tcm.getSelectionModel().removeListSelectionListener(this);
6673                }
6674                if (newValue != null && newValue instanceof TableColumnModel) {
6675                    TableColumnModel tcm = (TableColumnModel) newValue;
6676                    tcm.addColumnModelListener(this);
6677                    tcm.getSelectionModel().addListSelectionListener(this);
6678                }
6679
6680                // re-se cellEditor listeners
6681            } else if (name.compareTo("tableCellEditor") == 0) {
6682
6683                if (oldValue != null && oldValue instanceof TableCellEditor) {
6684                    ((TableCellEditor) oldValue).removeCellEditorListener(this);
6685                }
6686                if (newValue != null && newValue instanceof TableCellEditor) {
6687                    ((TableCellEditor) newValue).addCellEditorListener(this);
6688                }
6689            }
6690        }
